 Appendix A Verifying the ansatz validity for a larger system using tensor networks

 In this appendix, we study the applicability of our wave-packet ansatz to a larger system than considered in Sec.  II.3 .
We consider the Z 2 subscript 𝑍 2 Z_{2} italic_Z start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 2 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT LGT on a lattice with 26 staggered sites (13 physical sites) with the Brillouin zone Γ ~ = { − 6 ⁢ π 13 , − 5 ⁢ π 13 , ⋯ , 6 ⁢ π 13 } ~ Γ 6 𝜋 13 5 𝜋 13 ⋯ 6 𝜋 13 \tilde{\Gamma}=\{-\frac{6\pi}{13},-\frac{5\pi}{13},\cdots,\frac{6\pi}{13}\} over~ start_ARG roman_Γ end_ARG = { - divide start_ARG 6 italic_π end_ARG start_ARG 13 end_ARG , - divide start_ARG 5 italic_π end_ARG start_ARG 13 end_ARG , ⋯ , divide start_ARG 6 italic_π end_ARG start_ARG 13 end_ARG } .
The true momentum eigenstates, while cannot be obtained by exact diagonalization due to the size of the Hilbert space, can be approximated with a matrix product states (MPS) ansatz on a tensor network.
Using the density-matrix-renormalization-group (DMRG) optimization, one can obtain | Ω ⟩ MPS subscript ket Ω MPS \ket{\Omega}_{\rm MPS} | start_ARG roman_Ω end_ARG ⟩ start_POSTSUBSCRIPT roman_MPS end_POSTSUBSCRIPT that recovers the exact interacting ground state | Ω ⟩ ket Ω \ket{\Omega} | start_ARG roman_Ω end_ARG ⟩ with high precision in (1+1)D.
Excited states can also be built successively using the same DMRG process upon constraining the output to be orthogonal to the ground state and all other excited states with lower energy, if any.
The MPS states are further constrained such that the total fermionic excitation remains in the Q = N P 𝑄 subscript 𝑁 𝑃 Q=N_{P} italic_Q = italic_N start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_P end_POSTSUBSCRIPT sector, and thus the gauge symmetry is guaranteed on a periodic lattice.
All DMRG calculations in this work are carried out using the ITensors library  Fishman  et al. ( 2022 ) . 

 The DMRG calculations for the ground state and the 13 excited states with the lowest energy in each momentum sector are performed for a range of ( m f , ϵ ) subscript 𝑚 𝑓 italic-ϵ (m_{f},\epsilon) ( italic_m start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_f end_POSTSUBSCRIPT , italic_ϵ ) values.
In each DMRG optimization, the maximum allowed bond dimension is set to 600, and the Schmidt coefficients under 10 − 12 superscript 10 12 10^{-12} 10 start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT - 12 end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT are truncated.
The number of sweeps is set to 𝒪 ⁢ ( 100 ) 𝒪 100 \mathcal{O}(100) caligraphic_O ( 100 ) to ensure convergence in energy.
To further verify the quality of an output DMRG state | ψ ⟩ MPS subscript ket 𝜓 MPS \ket{\psi}_{\rm MPS} | start_ARG italic_ψ end_ARG ⟩ start_POSTSUBSCRIPT roman_MPS end_POSTSUBSCRIPT , the variance of energy is calculated:

Circuits for general j 𝑗 j italic_j can be constructed similarly. 

 The fidelity of the ansatz scanning over different m f subscript 𝑚 𝑓 m_{f} italic_m start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_f end_POSTSUBSCRIPT and ϵ italic-ϵ \epsilon italic_ϵ values is demonstrated in Fig.  11 .
Similar to the parameter scan on a smaller system in Sec.  II.3 , only non-negative momenta in the Brillouin zone are plotted for brevity. Similar fidelities are observed for negative-momentum eigenstates.
Again, the ansatz performs better in the strong-coupling regime, and the order-by-order improvement is visible. Here, the system size is large enough such that the non-mesonic excitations have energy well above that of the | k = 0 ⟩ ket 𝑘 0 \ket{k=0} | start_ARG italic_k = 0 end_ARG ⟩ eigenstate, and thus the cyan contour in Fig.  1 is not present.
The 3 3 3 3 rd order ansatz is able to achieve F > 0.99 𝐹 0.99 F>0.99 italic_F > 0.99 , except for the highest momentum | k = 6 ⁢ π 13 ⟩ ket 𝑘 6 𝜋 13 \ket{k=\frac{6\pi}{13}} | start_ARG italic_k = divide start_ARG 6 italic_π end_ARG start_ARG 13 end_ARG end_ARG ⟩ for a small parameter range.
Specifically, for
 m f = 0.1 , 0.3 subscript 𝑚 𝑓 0.1 0.3 m_{f}=0.1,0.3 italic_m start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_f end_POSTSUBSCRIPT = 0.1 , 0.3 and ϵ = − 0.1 italic-ϵ 0.1 \epsilon=-0.1 italic_ϵ = - 0.1 , there are excited states in other momentum sectors (above the single-particle eigenstate) with energy very similar to that of | | k | = 6 ⁢ π 13 ⟩ ket 𝑘 6 𝜋 13 \ket{|k|=\frac{6\pi}{13}} | start_ARG | italic_k | = divide start_ARG 6 italic_π end_ARG start_ARG 13 end_ARG end_ARG ⟩ . It is difficult for the DMRG to discern these from the eigenstates in the | k | = 6 ⁢ π 13 𝑘 6 𝜋 13 |k|=\frac{6\pi}{13} | italic_k | = divide start_ARG 6 italic_π end_ARG start_ARG 13 end_ARG sector. As a result, the orthogonality originally assumed for the states in Eq. ( 43 ) is not strictly valid, i.e., | ψ 1 / 2 ⟩ ket subscript 𝜓 1 2 \ket{\psi_{1/2}} | start_ARG italic_ψ start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 1 / 2 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT end_ARG ⟩ have overlap to states not in the k = 6 ⁢ π 13 𝑘 6 𝜋 13 k=\frac{6\pi}{13} italic_k = divide start_ARG 6 italic_π end_ARG start_ARG 13 end_ARG sector.
Ideally, a translationally invariant MPS ansatz based on quasiparticle excitations can do a better job at yielding the momentum eigenstates  Haegeman  et al. ( 2013 ); Zauner-Stauber  et al. ( 2018 ); Haegeman  et al. ( 2012 ); Belyansky  et al. ( 2024 ) . 

 We conclude that the momentum eigenstates can be faithfully be built from a finite-order ansatz of this work even in larger systems, although for verification purposes, better MPS ansatzes may be needed for large values of momenta to allow a fidelity test. 

 Appendix B Circuit for 𝒬 WP subscript 𝒬 WP \mathcal{Q}_{\rm WP} caligraphic_Q start_POSTSUBSCRIPT roman_WP end_POSTSUBSCRIPT in the minimal-gauge formalism

 The real (Re) and imaginary (Im) parts of 𝒜 ⁢ ( t ) 𝒜 𝑡 \mathcal{A}(t) caligraphic_A ( italic_t ) can be computed using a standard Hadamard test.
The state | Ψ 1 , Ψ 2 ⟩ ⊗ | 0 a t ⟩ tensor-product ket subscript Ψ 1 subscript Ψ 2 ket subscript 0 subscript 𝑎 𝑡 \ket{\Psi_{1},\Psi_{2}}\otimes\ket{0_{a_{t}}} | start_ARG roman_Ψ start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT , roman_Ψ start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 2 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT end_ARG ⟩ ⊗ | start_ARG 0 start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_a start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_t end_POSTSUBSCRIPT end_POSTSUBSCRIPT end_ARG ⟩ is first acted with a Hadamard gate on the ancilla a t subscript 𝑎 𝑡 a_{t} italic_a start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_t end_POSTSUBSCRIPT , followed by a controlled U ⁢ ( t ) 𝑈 𝑡 U(t) italic_U ( italic_t ) operation upon the | 1 ⟩ ket 1 \ket{1} | start_ARG 1 end_ARG ⟩ state of the ancilla.
Finally, a Hadamard or an R 𝐱 ⁢ ( π 4 ) superscript 𝑅 𝐱 𝜋 4 R^{\bf x}(\frac{\pi}{4}) italic_R start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT bold_x end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ( divide start_ARG italic_π end_ARG start_ARG 4 end_ARG ) gate is acted on the ancilla to obtain the real or imaginary parts, respectively.
Denote by p 0 subscript 𝑝 0 p_{0} italic_p start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 0 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT and p 1 subscript 𝑝 1 p_{1} italic_p start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT the probability for the ancilla to be measured in state | 0 a t ⟩ ket subscript 0 subscript 𝑎 𝑡 \ket{0_{a_{t}}} | start_ARG 0 start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_a start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_t end_POSTSUBSCRIPT end_POSTSUBSCRIPT end_ARG ⟩ and | 1 a t ⟩ ket subscript 1 subscript 𝑎 𝑡 \ket{1_{a_{t}}} | start_ARG 1 start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_a start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_t end_POSTSUBSCRIPT end_POSTSUBSCRIPT end_ARG ⟩ , respectively.
Then the quantity p 0 − p 1 subscript 𝑝 0 subscript 𝑝 1 p_{0}-p_{1} italic_p start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 0 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT - italic_p start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT obtains the real or the imaginary part out of the respective circuits.
The circuit for controlled U ⁢ ( t ) 𝑈 𝑡 U(t) italic_U ( italic_t ) can be obtained by controlling each block in Fig.  5 upon the state of the ancilla at every Trotter step.
The controlled e − i ⁢ δ ⁢ t ⁢ H h superscript 𝑒 𝑖 𝛿 𝑡 superscript 𝐻 ℎ e^{-i\delta tH^{h}} italic_e start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT - italic_i italic_δ italic_t italic_H start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_h end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT and e − i ⁢ δ ⁢ t ⁢ H m superscript 𝑒 𝑖 𝛿 𝑡 superscript 𝐻 𝑚 e^{-i\delta tH^{m}} italic_e start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT - italic_i italic_δ italic_t italic_H start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_m end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT circuits are given by controlling every constituent gate, while the controlled e − i ⁢ δ ⁢ t ⁢ H ϵ superscript 𝑒 𝑖 𝛿 𝑡 superscript 𝐻 italic-ϵ e^{-i\delta tH^{\epsilon}} italic_e start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT - italic_i italic_δ italic_t italic_H start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_ϵ end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT is obtained by replacing the R 𝐳 superscript 𝑅 𝐳 R^{\bf z} italic_R start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT bold_z end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT gates with their controlled versions. This is because in the absence of the R 𝐳 superscript 𝑅 𝐳 R^{\bf z} italic_R start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT bold_z end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT gates in the circuit in Fig.  5 (b), the collective action of the entangling gates is an identity on the state of fermion and the boson qubits. 

 Appendix E Time evolution of local observable for N P subscript 𝑁 𝑃 N_{P} italic_N start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_P end_POSTSUBSCRIPT =13

 [MATH:Refer to caption] 
 Figure 15: Shown are the staggered density χ n subscript 𝜒 𝑛 \chi_{n} italic_χ start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_n end_POSTSUBSCRIPT corresponding to four instances of time during the evolution, plotted against the lattice-site index n 𝑛 n italic_n .
The values of χ n subscript 𝜒 𝑛 \chi_{n} italic_χ start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_n end_POSTSUBSCRIPT agree well with the ideal result for both Appxs I and II. These are to be compared with the return-probability results plotted in Fig.  10 , which exhibit a significant deviation for Appx II.

 In Fig.  10 of the main text, we presented the results for the return probability ℛ ⁢ ( t ) ℛ 𝑡 \mathcal{R}(t) caligraphic_R ( italic_t ) for an N P = 13 subscript 𝑁 𝑃 13 N_{P}=13 italic_N start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_P end_POSTSUBSCRIPT = 13 system obtained from the MPS ansatz, as well as Appxs I and II using the noiseless Aer emulator. We observed significant deviation in this non-local quantity for the cruder Appx II, possibly due to large interference effects. In this appendix, we consider time evolution of the staggered density χ n subscript 𝜒 𝑛 \chi_{n} italic_χ start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_n end_POSTSUBSCRIPT instead, to investigate if the same deviation is seen for a local quantity. 

 To enable this comparison, we set all the simulation parameters identical to those in Fig.  10 , i.e., Trotter time step δ ⁢ t = 0.25 𝛿 𝑡 0.25 \delta t=0.25 italic_δ italic_t = 0.25 with 5 × 10 5 5 superscript 10 5 5\times 10^{5} 5 × 10 start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT 5 end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT shots for the noiseless emulator.
The results for χ n subscript 𝜒 𝑛 \chi_{n} italic_χ start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_n end_POSTSUBSCRIPT are shown in Fig.  15 at four different values of time, t ∈ { 1 , 4 , 6 , 11 } 𝑡 1 4 6 11 t\in\{1,4,6,11\} italic_t ∈ { 1 , 4 , 6 , 11 } .
These sample values of t 𝑡 t italic_t are chosen to compare χ n subscript 𝜒 𝑛 \chi_{n} italic_χ start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_n end_POSTSUBSCRIPT when return probability for Appx II shows relatively large deviation from its ideal result (exhibiting 15% to 30% relative errors).
As is observed, this local observable shows very small deviation from the ideal result for both Appxs I and II, confirming that local observables are more robust to small differences in initial states. 

 Appendix F Pauli twirling and operator decoherence renormalization

 In this appendix, we describe and implement a noise-mitigation strategy for obtaining the values of E = ⟨ σ ~ 𝐳 ⟩ 𝐸 expectation superscript ~ 𝜎 𝐳 E=\braket{\tilde{\sigma}^{\bf z}} italic_E = ⟨ start_ARG over~ start_ARG italic_σ end_ARG start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT bold_z end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT end_ARG ⟩ under the Trotter time evolution.
The results for this quantity are obtained from runs on the IonQ Forte quantum computer using Appx II, and are displayed in cyan triangles in Fig.  9 and below in Fig.  16 . These results clearly show significant error in this quantity. Even at t = 1 𝑡 1 t=1 italic_t = 1 , the value deviates from the ideal result, and it quickly diverges further away from the ideal values during the evolution. On the other hand, as was seen in in Fig.  7 , there exists reasonable agreement between hardware and simulator results for this quantity at t = 0 𝑡 0 t=0 italic_t = 0 (i.e., after the wave-packets’ preparation). We, therefore, conjuncture that the error in the time-evolved observable results from the larger number of entangling gates applied to the boson qubit compared to fermionic qubits, see Fig.  5 (b). 

 The desired result could be recovered, nonetheless, by executing a few additional noise-mitigating circuits, as shown in Fig.  16 , and described below: 

 [MATH:Refer to caption] 
 Figure 16: Shown are the noise-mitigated result obtained from Pauli twirling followed by operator decoherence renormalization (ODR) for the electric field at the boson qubit, E 𝐸 E italic_E , after two-wave-packet state evolution for time t 𝑡 t italic_t in the N P subscript 𝑁 𝑃 N_{P} italic_N start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_P end_POSTSUBSCRIPT system (compare with Fig.  9 ). The inverted magenta triangles are the results from the Pauli-twirled U ⁢ ( t ) 𝑈 𝑡 U(t) italic_U ( italic_t ) circuits. The black crosses are the Pauli-twirled identity circuits, U ⁢ ( 0 ) 𝑈 0 U(0) italic_U ( 0 ) , with similar structure as U ⁢ ( t ) 𝑈 𝑡 U(t) italic_U ( italic_t ) . Both of these results were obtained using the noisy emulator for the IonQ Forte quantum computer using 3000 shots.
The error bars obtained from 1000 bootstrap samples are smaller than the markers, and thus, they are not shown here.
The latter is used to scale the values associated with the inverted magenta triangles to the ODR results, denoted here by blue stars, and the error bars are obtained through error propagation. The results from the IonQ Forte device (cyan stars), which were calculated after removing Q̸ italic-Q̸ \not{Q} italic_Q̸ and a̸ italic-a̸ \not{a} italic_a̸ errors during post-processing, are also shown for comparison.

 Pauli twirling: Using the noisy emulator provided by IonQ for their Forte class devices, we execute 3000 shots for each Trotter step. These are then split over 10 equivalent “Pauli-twirled” circuits, and the final result is computed over the aggregated set of shots.
Each Pauli-twirled circuit is obtained by randomly picking one of the following equivalent operations for each CNOT gate in the e − i ⁢ δ ⁢ t ⁢ H ϵ superscript 𝑒 𝑖 𝛿 𝑡 superscript 𝐻 italic-ϵ e^{-i\delta tH^{\epsilon}} italic_e start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT - italic_i italic_δ italic_t italic_H start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_ϵ end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT block: 9 9 9 We chose these CNOT gates because the majority of entangling gates acting on the boson qubit belong to e − i ⁢ δ ⁢ t ⁢ H ϵ superscript 𝑒 𝑖 𝛿 𝑡 superscript 𝐻 italic-ϵ e^{-i\delta tH^{\epsilon}} italic_e start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT - italic_i italic_δ italic_t italic_H start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_ϵ end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT . CNOT, ( σ 𝐳 ⊗ I ~ ) tensor-product superscript 𝜎 𝐳 ~ 𝐼 (\sigma^{\bf z}\otimes\tilde{I}) ( italic_σ start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT bold_z end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ⊗ over~ start_ARG italic_I end_ARG ) CNOT ( σ 𝐳 ⊗ I ~ ) tensor-product superscript 𝜎 𝐳 ~ 𝐼 (\sigma^{\bf z}\otimes\tilde{I}) ( italic_σ start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT bold_z end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ⊗ over~ start_ARG italic_I end_ARG ) , ( σ 𝐱 ⊗ I ~ ) tensor-product superscript 𝜎 𝐱 ~ 𝐼 (\sigma^{\bf x}\otimes\tilde{I}) ( italic_σ start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT bold_x end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ⊗ over~ start_ARG italic_I end_ARG ) CNOT ( σ 𝐱 ⊗ σ ~ 𝐱 ) tensor-product superscript 𝜎 𝐱 superscript ~ 𝜎 𝐱 (\sigma^{\bf x}\otimes\tilde{\sigma}^{\bf x}) ( italic_σ start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT bold_x end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ⊗ over~ start_ARG italic_σ end_ARG start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT bold_x end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ) , and ( σ 𝐱 ⊗ σ ~ 𝐲 ) tensor-product superscript 𝜎 𝐱 superscript ~ 𝜎 𝐲 (\sigma^{\bf x}\otimes\tilde{\sigma}^{\bf y}) ( italic_σ start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT bold_x end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ⊗ over~ start_ARG italic_σ end_ARG start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT bold_y end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ) CNOT ( σ 𝐲 ⊗ σ ~ 𝐳 ) tensor-product superscript 𝜎 𝐲 superscript ~ 𝜎 𝐳 (\sigma^{\bf y}\otimes\tilde{\sigma}^{\bf z}) ( italic_σ start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT bold_y end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ⊗ over~ start_ARG italic_σ end_ARG start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT bold_z end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ) .
Here, tilde operators act on the boson qubit.
This process converts the coherent noise into a decoherent noise. As shown in Fig.  16 , Pauli-twirled results (inverted magenta triangles) improve the results and, in particular, fix the shifted value at t = 1 𝑡 1 t=1 italic_t = 1 . This implies that the uniform offset for all time steps likely is caused by coherent errors in the device. 

 Operator decoherence renormalization (ODR): Next, we apply a procedure called ODR, which involves scaling the value of the observable E 𝐸 E italic_E as E ODR ⁢ ( t ) = E ⁢ ( t ) / ( 1 − ρ ⁢ ( t ) ) subscript 𝐸 ODR 𝑡 𝐸 𝑡 1 𝜌 𝑡 E_{\rm ODR}(t)=E(t)/(1-\rho(t)) italic_E start_POSTSUBSCRIPT roman_ODR end_POSTSUBSCRIPT ( italic_t ) = italic_E ( italic_t ) / ( 1 - italic_ρ ( italic_t ) ) . The scaling factor ρ ⁢ ( t ) 𝜌 𝑡 \rho(t) italic_ρ ( italic_t ) is obtained by executing a circuit for each Trotter time t 𝑡 t italic_t with a similar structure as the target circuit but whose output is known.
We obtain ρ ⁢ ( t ) 𝜌 𝑡 \rho(t) italic_ρ ( italic_t ) by executing the Pauli-twirled circuits for the U ⁢ ( 0 ) 𝑈 0 U(0) italic_U ( 0 ) operator, and demand that the value of E 𝐸 E italic_E remains the same as its value E 0 subscript 𝐸 0 E_{0} italic_E start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 0 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT at t = 0 𝑡 0 t=0 italic_t = 0 [shown in Fig.  7 (a)].
The U ⁢ ( 0 ) 𝑈 0 U(0) italic_U ( 0 ) circuit can be executed by setting δ ⁢ t → − δ ⁢ t → 𝛿 𝑡 𝛿 𝑡 \delta t\to-\delta t italic_δ italic_t → - italic_δ italic_t in the last two circuit blocks in Fig.  5 (a) and using ϵ = 0 italic-ϵ 0 \epsilon=0 italic_ϵ = 0 for the middle block. The U ⁢ ( 0 ) 𝑈 0 U(0) italic_U ( 0 ) circuits blocks are implemented n t subscript 𝑛 𝑡 n_{t} italic_n start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_t end_POSTSUBSCRIPT times, where n t subscript 𝑛 𝑡 n_{t} italic_n start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_t end_POSTSUBSCRIPT is the number of Trotter steps up to time t 𝑡 t italic_t . The value of E ′ ⁢ ( t ) = ⟨ σ ~ 𝐳 ⁢ ( t ) ⟩ superscript 𝐸 ′ 𝑡 expectation superscript ~ 𝜎 𝐳 𝑡 E^{\prime}(t)=\braket{\tilde{\sigma}^{\bf z}(t)} italic_E start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ′ end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ( italic_t ) = ⟨ start_ARG over~ start_ARG italic_σ end_ARG start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT bold_z end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ( italic_t ) end_ARG ⟩ for these circuits are shown by the black plus sign in Fig.  16 . Note that since the electric-field value at the boson qubit does not change significantly during the time evolution, E ′ ⁢ ( t ) superscript 𝐸 ′ 𝑡 E^{\prime}(t) italic_E start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ′ end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ( italic_t ) is nearly identical to E ⁢ ( t ) 𝐸 𝑡 E(t) italic_E ( italic_t ) . The scaling factor ρ ⁢ ( t ) 𝜌 𝑡 \rho(t) italic_ρ ( italic_t ) is now obtained from these results, and from E 0 subscript 𝐸 0 E_{0} italic_E start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 0 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT , via the relation ρ ⁢ ( t ) = 1 − E ′ ⁢ ( t ) / E 0 𝜌 𝑡 1 superscript 𝐸 ′ 𝑡 subscript 𝐸 0 \rho(t)=1-E^{\prime}(t)/E_{0} italic_ρ ( italic_t ) = 1 - italic_E start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ′ end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ( italic_t ) / italic_E start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 0 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT . We then apply the same scaling factor ρ ⁢ ( t ) 𝜌 𝑡 \rho(t) italic_ρ ( italic_t ) to obtain E ODR subscript 𝐸 ODR E_{\rm ODR} italic_E start_POSTSUBSCRIPT roman_ODR end_POSTSUBSCRIPT out of E ⁢ ( t ) 𝐸 𝑡 E(t) italic_E ( italic_t ) , the results of which are shown as blue stars in Fig.  16 . These results are in much better agreement with the ideal values than unmitigated results, proving the effectiveness of these mitigation strategies in this simulation. 

 This analysis is performed on the IonQ Forte emulator instead of the IonQ Forte quantum system due to the limited hardware access. It would be interesting to see if this procedure also works for the actual hardware data.
